PRIORACTION 1-BUDGETEXECUTIONAND MTEF

Proposedprior action

            Budget compositionand compliance                        PEAPObjective 1.1

Inthe PublicExpenditureReview,the Governmenthas agreed    Reducingpublic expenditureas a
with donors onthe Medium-TermExpenditureFrameworkfor      percentageof GDP throughbudget
2007/08 to 2009/10, andhas executedthe FY2006/07budget    rationalization.
consistent withthe budget allocation as appropriatedand
adjustedwiththe approval ofParliament.


Expectationsof the prioraction
Overall expenditures should be within the Approved Budget and programmed levels,
adjusted for anywithin-year domestic revenue performance, inFY2006/07.

The Government will ensure that PAF expenditures perform at a minimumo f95 percent o f
the Approved Budget inFY2006/07.

Government will also limit supplementary requests to Parliament by the security andpublic
administration sectors to those that can be accommodated within the resources
appropriated to those sectors in the Approved Budget (presented in June and approved by
Parliament). The Government will gradually reduce the share o f public administration
(PRSC definition) in the GOU budget by 0.5 o f a percentage point per annum over the
period FY2006/07 to FY2008/09. Public administration agencies to be monitored under
this prior action include the Office o f the Prime Minister (excluding Development);
Foreign Affairs and Missions Abroad; NPA; URA; State House; Public Service
Commission; Local Government (excluding Development); Local Government Finance
Commission; Office o f the President (excluding ISO/ESO and Ethics and Integrity);
specified officers salaries; Parliamentary Commission; the Uganda Human Rights
Commission; and the Electoral Commission.

Monitoringthe budget
As has been the case in the past, progress and consistency o f budget execution will
continue to be monitored through preparation o f quarterly outturns which are shared with
the development partners through the PERWorking Group.

Furthermore, the semi-annual and annual budget performance reports highlighting both
financial and physical achievement will be prepared and published as part o f our
commitment to ensure transparency inbudget execution. Monitoring reports should aim to
show budget execution (i)as a percentage o f amounts originally approved; (ii)as a
percentage o f amounts approved and adjusted through supplements; and (iii)          on a cash
limit as well as pro-ratabasis.




                                                   117

PRIORACTION 2 -INVESTMENTCLIMATE

Ugandaranked 118 in2007 out o f 178 economies inthe cost o f doing business report 2008,
slipping marginally but consistently when compared with the 2007 and 2006 rankings (107
o f 175 economies in the 2007 report). However, over this period Uganda successfully
reformed and adopted new Labor laws, an areawhere Governments tend to increase rigidity,
thus maintaining Uganda's best ranking in Africa at llth, the cost o f doingReducing
business by easing entry and exit regulations and eliminating unnecessary red tape remains
the main activity for Government's engagement in the private sector, directly related to
increased job creation and poverty reduction in Uganda. The Government has formed a
coordinated approach which should lead to a consistent improvement o f the investment
climate and to the realization of the PEAP Pillar 2 objectives. The Investment Climate
issues are highlightedwithin the Competitiveness and Investment Climate Strategy 2006-
2010 (CICS), which replaced the Medium-Term Competitiveness Strategy 2000-2005 and,
in line with the PEAP, encompasses government policies in support of an efficient and
competitive private sector. A formal dialogue between the Government and the private
sector chaired by the President o f Uganda (PIRT) provides guidance on priorities and
monitories the success o f the proposed reforms. The priorities areas are in infrastructure,
land reform, business environment and the financial sector.

The CICS matrix summarizes these actions (see draft annualized matrix), as sub set o f
which were taken as the basis for undertakings for the PRSC. For PRSC7, the following
undertakings were agreedupon:

       (i)      The Companies bill and Insolvency Billhavebeen approved by Cabinet and
       presentedto Parliament;

     (ii)       The Policy Paper on Pension Reform hasbeenpresented to and approved by
     Cabinet


       Thejustification for focusing on these undertakings is highlighted below.

Companies bill andInsolvencybill
The Companies bill and Insolvency bill have been approved by Cabinet and presented to
Parliament.

Statementof the problem. The company's act is the key legislative piece that impact's the
ease o f establishing a business, the number o f procedures, capital requirements, the cost to
register, protection for investors, etc. Business exit, in particular voluntary business exit i s
important to reallocating resources efficiently. Business entry and exit regulations raises the
rates o f new business creation, encourages formalization leading to better access to finance
andmore formal sectorjobs.

The proposed reform sets out only two procedures for registration (submission o f
memorandum of association (and articles if any) and statutory de~laration)~~.              Onregistration

35 Though see Section 191o f draft Act that has additional registrationrequirements for PLC's.


                                                    118

 o f the memorandum o f association the registrar issues a certificate o f incorporation. The
 certificate i s conclusive evidence that all requirements relating to registration have been
 complied with by the company and the company is hlly functional from the date of issue o f
 the certificate (section 19(2)). There is no paid-in minimumcapital requirement to act as a
 barrier. The time required to complete each procedure is not set out inthe Bill. This is not
 unusual language for Company law- since registrars are reluctant to be under a legal
 obligation to register within a certain time. However, the Ugandan Government might
 consider following the language used section 13 o f New Zealand's Companies Act 1993
 which states that: "As soon as the Registrar receives a properly completed application for
 registration o f a company, the registrar must register the application and issue a certificate
 o f incorporation". The reforms also provide for winding up or liquidation arrangements on a
 voluntary basis which are the standard arrangements consistent with general practice. The
reformprocess i s on track to reduce time and procedures to establish and close a business.

 Objective of the undertaking. The objective o f this undertaking within the investment
 climate prior action i s to ensure that the Government takes the necessary steps to accelerate
 enactment o f the Companies bill and the Insolvency bill with a view to ease and reduce the
cost o f doing business inUganda.

Milestone                               Timeline                      MOV

                                                   Dabinet.

                                                   to Parliament.



Policypaperon PensionReform
The policypaper on Pension Reform hasbeenpresented to andapproved bythe Cabinet.

Statement of the problem. Access and cost o f finance is a persistent constraint to
enterprise growth reported by enterprises in the I C A 2006 and 2004. The Government
embarked on a series o f reforms to increase access to finance by establishing the legal
framework for the credit reference bureau inUganda, improving the capital markets and by
reforming the pension funds. Following the completion o f the legal framework for Credit
reference Bureaus and the issue o f one license in2007, further focus on pensionreform was
expected. Uganda's pension system i s yet to evolve into a system that could allow for
provision of adequate, affordable, and sustainable retirement incomes; stimulate domestic
savings; contribute to the development o f the market for longer-term finance and hence
stimulate economic growth. Inits current state, the system covers no more than 5 percent o f
the population and has accumulated assets o f about 4 percent o f GDP. The system i s
afflicted by a host o f problems ranging from governance and management problems to
issues o f sustainability and lack o f appropriate supervision.



                                               119

The pension reform agenda has been under discussion for a number o f years, with fairly
comprehensive national consultations completed in 2004 by a Pension Reform Taskforce.
Oversight o f a pension sector operating within a liberalized environment would require the
introduction o f new governance and supervisory structures, which are nonexistent today.
The reform process therefore needs a framework that provides an independent regulator,
reform and restructuring o f the National Social Security Fund, and liberalization o f the
sector, with the particular objective o f expanding efficient fund management capacity. The
reform process would also aim to ensure that the public pension scheme is funded in a
more sustainable manner. Within the CICS (2006-2010), key actions identified to move
this process forward included: (i)      presentation to Parliament o f a pension sector reform
policy; (ii) establishment o f an appropriate regulatory framework; (iii)         development and
implementation o f a sectoral development strategy; and (iv) restructuringand strengthening
o f the National Social Security Fund. The Government o f Uganda recently prepared a
policy paper on pension regulation to be approved by cabinet in February which is not an
overall policy paper on the pension reform as envisaged. However given the complex
nature o f these reforms, it i s commendable that the Government regained some momentum
inrestartingthe policydialogue onpensionreform.

Objective of the undertaking. The objective o f the undertaking within the investment
climate prior action i s to ensure that the Government takes the necessary steps to accelerate
the pension reform agenda by urgently completing nationwide consensus building on the
agenda and ensuringthat the agreedpolicyhas beenapproved by cabinet to pave the way to
begin reforms.

PRIOR ACTION 4 -PUBLIC FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT




       Proposed PRSC 7 Prior Actions for Public FinancialManagement,February 2008

        The following are actions concerning improvements in financial management, which were
        discussed and agreed during the PRSC Appraisal Mission of January 2008. These are aimed
        at makingavailable informationand data on public spending, improvingpayroll controls and payroll
        audits, financial reportingand auditsof parastatals, clearingof backlogof Treasury Memoranda, and
        the legalframeworkandmanagementofprocurement.

        1.o    BudgetReporting
        1.1    Ministry of Finance produces budget execution reports for the first quarter, semi-
               annual, third quarter and annual periods of the financial year that cover the following
               items Ministry wise: budget allocations, quarterly ceiling, budget releases, and actual
               quarterly expenditures.The semi annual andannual reportswill be publishedwithin 30
               days of the end of the reporting period. In addition COFOG wise quarterly actual
               expenditureswill be made available within 30 days following the end of the reporting
               periodstarting with the quarter ended30th September2007.

        1.2    These reports will be in addition to the existing six monthly budget performance
               reportswhich include reportingagainst the MTEF andperformanceindicators.

        1.3    Ministry of Finance to provide the Bank with the budget execution report for the
               quarter ended 30th September 2007 and the semi-annual period ended 31st December
               2007 by the endof January 2008.
       2.0     ImprovementsinPavroll Controls
       2.1     In order to ensure effective payroll controls, the Inspectorate and Internal Audit
               department audits payrolls as an ongoing activity for all ministries (except for the
               armed forces of the Ministry of Defence). Weaknesses in the process are highlighted
               for managementattention.

       2.2     Government committed to undertake a comprehensive internal audit of the payroll by
               31January 2008 for all ministriesexcept Ministry ofDefense (armed forces payroll). It
               i s also planned these comprehensive payroll audits are undertaken after every two
               years thereafter. Appropriate action will be taken to address the recommendations
               arising out ofthe payrollaudits.

       2.3     A consolidatedreport for the payroll audit for the quarter July to September 2007 has
               beenpreparedfor 31 out of 33 ministries, departments and agencies. The payroll audit
               for State House and Ministry of Information and CommunicationTechnology are yet
               to be concluded. In addition, arrangements are beingto audit the Ministryof Defence
               (civilian staff)which hadearlierbeenexcludedfrom the list to be audited.

       2.4     Accountant General's Officewill follow up the issues raisedin the payroll audits with
               the AccountingOfficers ofthe audited entities.


       3.0    Law for the Office of the Auditor General
       3.1    The Audit Bill was approvedby Cabinet on 30 May2007 and presentedto Parliament
              in August 2007. It was expected that the Audit Billwould be passedby Parliament into
              law by 31 December 2007, andthe Audit Boardsetup by 30 June 2008.

       3.2    Audit bill was presented to Parliamenton 28 August 2007. The Billwas expectedto be
              passed by Parliament by end of January 2008 but due to CHOGM and the recess
              period ending early February, the bill is now expected to be passed by end of March
              2008 andthe Audit Boardestablishedby 30 June 2008.

                                                      122

4.0  Reports of Parastatah
4.1  Government committed to ensure that 100% of parastatals/state enterprises receiving
     funding from the consolidated fbnd account submit their accounts for audit within the
     statutory time frame beginningwith the 2006/07 accounts.

4.2  In order to monitor the outstanding audits for all the parastatalslstateenterprisesup to
     2005/06, we prepared a statement at 30 September 2007 showing the status of
     submissions of accounts for audit, and issuance o f audit reports and audited financial
     statements for all parastatals with an indication of when the outstanding accounts will
     be submitted to the Auditor General for audit.

4.3  As at 31 January 2008, 28 out o f 35 parastatals that receive funding from the
     consolidated fimd (representing 80%) had submitted accounts for 2006107 to the Office
     of the Auditor General (OAG) for audit in accordance with the statutory requirements.
     GoU funding to the parastatals for FY 06/07 totaled Shs 74.4 billion out of which Shs
     5 billion (6.7%) represents the 7 parastatals that are yet to submit their accounts for
     audit. Arrangements have been made to follow up the remaining parastatalsto ensure
     the target of 100% submission of accountsto OAG is achieved.

5.0  PreDaration of Treasurv Memoranda
5.1  Government committed to ensure that the issue of outstanding Treasury Memoranda
     (TMs) for finalized PAC reports to Parliament is up-to-date by December 31, 2007.
     TMs for the PAC reports of 1999/00 and 2000/01 were yet to be submitted to
     Parliament at the time o f this mission. PAC expects TMs to be finalized within three
     months after they issue their report.

5.2  By 31 January 2008, the Treasury Memoranda for 1999/00 and 2000/01 had been
     published and are planned to be presentedto Parliament (by the Minister for Finance,
     Planningand Economic Development) during February2008.

5.3  Arrangements are in place to ensure the future PAC reports are attended to
     immediately they are released and a treasury memorandum prepared within three
     months ofreceipt.


6.0  Procurement
6.1 The prior action i s geared toward (i) revamping the legal framework that governs public
    procurement; and (ii) ensuring the establishment of functioning procurement and disposals
    units in Government bodies. Specifically, the agreedprior actionwordingreadas follows:

     (a)    The Ministry of Finance will cause the preparation of a draft for the revision of
            provisions in the public procurement law and regulations identified as deficient. The
            draft of the revisions will be subject to review and comments by the World Bank and
            will be approved by Cabinet by 31 January 2008. The Minister of Finance will
            thereafter follow up approval of the revisions by Parliament to be done as soon as
            possible.

    (b)     All PDEs inthe Ministries and Parastatal Organizations and at least 70 YOof PDEs in
            Local Authorities should each have Procurement and Disposals Unit (PDU) and a
            Contractscommitteeby January 31,2008.

    Revision of the Law
6.2 Significant progress has been made in drafting the necessary revisions to the law and
    regulations. However, it is considered necessary to provide for more time to ensure
    sufficient consultations with stakeholders. In this regard, a Technical Working Group
    (chaired by the Deputy Secretary to the Treasury) has been constituted including staff of
    PPDA, The Accountant General's Office, selected staff of other Government entities and
    privatesector representativesdc. as requiredto preparethe necessary revisions.

PRIORACTION 7-PUBLIC SERVICE REFORM

Anticipatedprior action
         Satisfactory progress in the implementation o f the new phase o f Public Service
Reform Program (PSRP) as evidenced by accomplishment o f the undertakings agreed to in
the Joint Government and Development Partners Review process, including specific
measures by the Government to: (i)      sanction those responsible for ghost workers on the
payroll; (ii) right-size the public service, and (iii) toward achieving medium-term
                                                       work
salary targets set inthe August 2006 public service pay reform policy.

Background
The Ministry o f Public Service (MoPS) has with the support o f development partners
embarked on implementation o f the third phase o f the Public Service Reform Program
(PSRP) 2005-2010. The PSRP was launched inOctober 2006 andprogress is observed ina
number o f strategic areas. These include, but are not limited to, enhancement o f the
demandside o f accountabilitythrough the development and use o fclient service charters in
MDAs and LGs; training for top and senior management inleadership inMDAs and LGs
under the leadership and change management initiative; setting up the structures for
implementation o f the Integrated Pay and Personnel System (IPPS); and restructuring o f
M D A s to better respond to their mandates.

To support PSRP implementation, MoPS has established institutional arrangements for a
joint GOU/development partners PSRP review process. This process will ensure adequate
monitoring o f and accountability for results, planning, and budgeting for the PSRP and
facilitate committing to sound indicators to reflect progress under PSRC7 andPSRC8.

The Public Sector Management Working Group (PSM WG) comprising the Office of the
PrimeMinister, Ministry o f Public Service, Ministryo f Local Government, Public Service
Commission, Local Government Finance Commission, and the National Planning
Authority is now operational. This provides an institutional framework to implement the
PSRP within the sector-wide approach.

Prior actionfor PRSC7
Under PRSC7 GOU will continue to monitor the implementation o f PSRP. Inthis regard,
GOU and development partners in November 2007 agreed on key priority interventions
that will seek to: (i)enhance the performance and accountability o f public service
organizations; (ii) attract and retain an adequatenumber o f skilled andable personnel inthe
public service; (iii) inplace a public service that i s efficient and affordable; (iv) provide
                     put
a public service that i s an enabling and empowering work environment; (v) motivate and
adequately remunerate public servants; and (vi) develop leadership and                 change
management skills throughout the public service.

Further, discussion o f the specific measures to achieve the objectives o f the medium-term
pay policy targets will be a central part o f the dialogue through the Public Sector
Management Working Group and annual reviews o f the PSRP. Special attention will be



                                              128

 paid to progress made by GOU to right-size and control the growth o f the public service
 with the aim o f achieving a leaner public service. Currently, MoPS and MoFPED are
 undertaking analytical work with a view to propose a road map for achieving enhanced
 public service pay based on the August 2006 Public Service Pay Policy targets and
 transformation o f the public service interms o f its capacity, culture, and performance. It is
 anticipated that this work will provide a critical input inthe ongoing initiatives aimed at re-
 orienting the public service and that it would serve to escalate both awareness and the
 policy dialogue on the trade-offs and interventions needed to attain top level commitment.

 At the same time, the government task force will continue working on specific measures
 that would achieve the medium-term public service pay targets. The task force i s
 considering measyres such as, but not limited to, (i)budget rationalization o f non-
 personnel expenditures that enhance remuneration leading to enhancing wage bill
 allocations in the MTEF to enable significant progress in implementation o f the medium-
 term pay targets; (ii) agreement on plans and numbers for salary enhancement in line with
 medium-term targets that would enhance pay across the public service in line with the
 medium-term targets to be implemented by 2008/09; and (iii)        a performance management
 regime covering all senior management in MDAs (UlE and above) promulgated to take
 effect byJuly 2008.

 The task team believed that it would be crucial to have in place a stringent performance
 management regime to be operationalized in tandem with pay enhancement. However, it
 might be premature, pending a more comprehensive and strategic analysis o f budgetary
 issues for the next MTEF, to presume the affordability o f a significantly enhanced wage
 bill allocation in the near future. Furthermore, prospects for significant pay enhancement
 across the public service remain tenuous. It i s expected that the government task team will
 continue to deepen its work to develop a clear plano f action to propose concrete measures
 based on their initial thinking.

 The recently completed PricewaterhouseCoopers study on Public Service Employment,
 Wage Bill Management and Pay Reform (commissioned jointly by MoPS and MoFPED)
 indicated that total public service employment (excluding defense personnel) was set to
rise from about 234,160 in June 2007 to about 263,822 in FY2011/12. However, with
 appropriate measures to right-size and control growth, change can be moderated so that the
total numberdoes not exceed 253,335 inFY2011/12.

There is already an ongoing exercise to review government structures. This process will
provide opportunities to reduce establishments and MoPS and MoFPED will communicate
and enforce hardceilings for annual recruitment.

Secondly, growth in the total number o f public service employees will be moderated by
implementing the recommendations o f various studies, reviews, and value for money
audits that examined affordability, cost efficiency, and effectiveness o f human resources
deployment and utilization inpriority social sectors, dating back to 2003 and including the
recently completed PER and the Education Efficiency Review. MoPS and MoFPED will
jointly synthesize these recommendations and champion their implementation through the
sector reviews.


                                              129

For PRSC7, MoPS and MoFPED have identified two measures that are achievable by the
time o f appraisal. These measureswill also be discussed duringthe PSRP annual review in
December 2007. These include: (i)implementation o f measures to right-size the public
service and control growth to the limit o f affordability while ensuring cost-effectiveness
and efficiency; and (ii)  launching measures agreed to improve planning and budgeting for
human resources. MoPS will issue a specific circular to MDAs providing guidance on
budgeting andplanningfor humanresources inFY 2008/09.

Means of verification

    (i)    The Aide Memoire o f the joint Public Service Reform Program Review,
           December 2007, providing details ofprogress toward the agreed indicators.

   (ii)    MoPS will issue a specific circular to MDAs providing guidance on budgeting
           and planningfor humanresources inFY 2008/09.

  (iii)    Table o f figures indicating potential savings achievable from strict budgetingfor
           humanresourcesbaedon staffinposts andtakinginto account the critical posts.




                                            130

Statement of the problem. Currently about 95 percent of LG financing is from central
government transfer. There is therefore a high rate o f dependence by LGs on central
government. This situation is not healthy for LGs under a policy o f devolution
decentralization. Over the last two years government has taken a number o f measures to
address these concerns which included (i)            enactment o f the LGs (Rating) Act, 2005; (ii)
financial support to LGs to implement their revenue enhancement plan; and (iii)            proposed
two new taxes (local Service Tax and Hotel Tax) to broaden LGrevenue base announced in
the budget speech o fFY2007/8.

Objective of the prior action. The objective o fthe prior action is to document andmonitor
the impact o f these interventions and their contribution to revenue growth controlled by
LGs.

Recruitmentofstrategiccore staffinginLGs
Statement of the problem. LGs were restructured in2005. Staffing level o f LGs currently
averages 35 percent o f the established posts. This low level o f staffing undermines LG
capability to deliver on their decentralized mandates. Current funding from central
government was only adequate to meet about 47 percent o f the LG wage bill. To address


                                                    131

this problem the FY2007/08 government budget provided an additional Ushs 33 billion
under the unconditional grant toward LG wage bill enhancement, which will raise LG
staffing from the current 35 percent to 65 percent o f the established posts. There i s therefore
a need for the MoLGMoPS to guide LGs and ensure that this money will be used to recruit
strategic and core staff who will improve LG capacity to deliver effectively and efficiently
on their mandates. This will bebased on the current staffing level andneeds o f each LG.

Objective of the prior action. The objective of the prior action is to ensure that adequate
guidance i s given from MoLG/MoPS to LGs in the effective use o f the Ushs 33 billion to
recruit strategic and core staff during the FY2007/08 based on the staffing status o f each
LG.

Enactmentof a law to promoteorganizedurbandevelopmentandhumansettlements
Statement of the problem.As observed under PRSC6, many towns and urban centers in
Uganda have degenerated in terms o f planning and infrastructure development. Immediate
policy actions and an enabling legal framework are needed in order to avert disastrous
consequences. Under PRSC6 the principles for the proposed new law were discussed and
approve by the Cabinet and a bill developed. The bill now needs to be presented to
Parliament for enactment into law to allow for the implementation and enforcement o f
organized urbandevelopment.

Objective of the prior action. The objective o f the prior action, as a follow on to PRSC6,
i s to develop a Physical Planning Bill which will comprehensively address the complex
problems o frapid urbanization

Monitoringof LGexpenditures of centralgovernment transfers
Statement of the problem. Although transfers from central government account for a
substantial amount o f LG budgets, currently there i s no mechanism to monitor the

need to monitor LGs expenditures from these transfers to ensure that they are consistent
with the PEAPobjectives.

Objective of the prior action. The objective o f the prior action is to ensure that

PRIORACTION 9 -EDUCATION

A. JOINTPOSITIONPAPER ONCRITICALAND PROCESSUNDERTAKINGS

B. FOR THENOVEMBER 2007ESR

1 .o  INTRODUCTION

1.1   This Position Paper on the Undertakings agreed upon at the November 2006
      Education Sector Review (ESR) i s hereby presented to the October 2007 ESR. It
      has beenagreedupon by representativesof the Government of Uganda (GOU) and
      those of the Education Funding Agencies Group (EFAG). It is recommended that
      this Position Paper be adopted by the Education Sector Review and incorporated
      into the November 2007 Education Sector Review Aide Memoire.

1.2   The Position Paper is dividedinto 2 parts:

      (a) Status of criticalundertakings; and,
      (b) Status ofprocessundertakings.

1.3   The undertakingsare the triggers for budget support andADB project support hnds

2.0   CRITICAL UNDERTAKINGS

2.1   PublicExpenditure

2.2.1 Implementationofrecommendationsof the most recent tracking study and
      outstandingissues from previous tracking studies inEducation.

(a)  How and WhenReported

     ProgressReport at November 2007 ESR.

(b)  Means of Verification

     Progressreport

( 4  Status

     The recent tracking studies conducted in the sector include; UPE Tracking Study
     2006, and a tracking study on utilization of resources in conflict areas 2005, the
     Study on Primary Teacher Recruitment, Deployment and Payroll Management
     2004, SFGValue for MoneyAudit 2003.




                                          134

      There has been substantial progress in implementing recommendations o f the
      previous tracking studies in the education sector. Pending actions to facilitate
       direct transfer o f per capita funds to primary schools would require amendment o f
       the law, and discussions inthis regard are at Cabinet level.


      Undertakingmet.

2.2   Quality enhancement indicators

      Government will implement actions to improve, measure andreport on the
      following indicators.

2.2.1 PupilTeacher Ratio calculated nationally andbydistrict: 51:1
      6,594,872 children assumedto be inGovernment schools and 129,000 teachersby
      June 2007.

(a)  How and WhenReported


      0  Progress Report at November 2007 ESR.
      0  MOPSto submit RegularReports to ESCC.

(b)  Means of VeriJication

     Progress report to November 2007.

(c)  Status

     The preliminary Annual School Census results for 2007 indicate that there are
      6,684,5 13 pupils enrolled in Government aided primary schools (with 3,355,213
     boys and 3,329,300 girls). In2005, the total establishment for primary teachers was
     capped at 129,000 teachers. However, the Ministryo f Public Service payroll returns
     for end o f June 2007 indicated that a total o f 128,262 teachers (Le. 99.43% o f the
     approved ceiling) had accessed the payroll. Therefore, based on the preliminary
     enrolment figures above, the PTR computes to 52:l.           This is higher than the
     targeted 51:l agreed during the 2006 ESSR. The increase in the ratio occurred
     because enrolment increase was higher than anticipated yet there was a cap on the
     number o fprimary school teachers for that period.

     Pupil Teacher Ratios calculated by district have in some cases improved, in others
     remained stable or have deteriorated, due in part to remoteness and difficult
     circumstances like insecurity.      The Ministry o f Public Service will continue to
     support those districts with large establishment gaps and report during the
     Education Sector Coordination Committee meetings.

     Undertakingmet at nationallevel. Undertakingpartiallymetat districtlevel,
     since there was no improvementinthe PTRof some districts.

         Pupil ClassroomRatio calculatednationally andby district: 76:1
         6,594,872 Children assumed to be in Government schools and a stock of 88,135
         classroomsconstructedby June 2007.

         How and When Reported

         ProgressReport at November 2007 ESR.

         Means of Verification

         Report to November 2007 ESR

         Status

         The stock o f classrooms increased from 86,530 (June 2006) to 88,135 (June 2007)
         an increase of 2%. Inthe same period, enrolment increasedfrom 6,5 19,063 (2006)
         to 6,684,513 (2007) resulting into a pupil classroom ratio of 76:l which was

         Primary Completion Rates for P738 54%
         We assume 478,697 will register for P7examinationswith an estimated
         883,699children aged 12years inthe population in2007, resulting into a

         How and When Reported

         Status

         Trend inthe completion rates for P7 for 2003-2006 is shown inTable 2



           Gendernear                    2005                    2006                    2007

           Boys                          54%                      53%                    49%
           Girls                         47%                      42%                    51%
          All                            51%                      48%                    50%


         Results from Table 2 indicate that the completion rates for P7 stagnated at around 50%
         despite the actions taken. Out of the assumed 478,697 candidates for PLE in2007,
         only 444,221 candidates registered. When the ministry noticed that the number of
         pupils who had registered for Primary Leaving Examinations (PLE) by May 2007
         haddeclined, the following additional actions were implemented.

        (i)CircularsweresenttoallChiefAdministrativeOfficers(CAOs)toinformhead
               teachers to allow all pupils who were in P7 to register for 2007 PLE. UNEB
               extended the deadline to the end o f August instead of May 31st. This resulted
               into an increase in the numbers from 432,128 who had registered in May to
               444,019, an increaseof 11,891 pupils.




38 Primary completion rate is d e f i e d as the total number o f pupils registered for registered for the PLE,
regardless o f age, expressed as a percentage of the population at the official primary graduation age.




                                                       138

       (ii)Adiagnostic studythatassessedcausesoflowcompletionwasconducted, and
              future actions for improving the primary completion rate will be based on this
              study. These actions will be discussed and prioritised at the next ESCC for
              implementationbefore the beginning o f the next school year - see table 9.

       While there has been a slight improvement in completion rates, the sector
       acknowledges that these rates are still unacceptably low and the target o f 54% was
       not met. This low rate calls for action by all key stakeholders to address the major
       causes o f low completion rate, and will be reflected in credible actions to address
       this situation.

      inEnglishinbothclasses, reflectedbythe increase inthe percentagesofpupilswith
      the desired rating.   These improvements could be attributed to the government
      policy aimed at not only supplying books to primary schools but also ensuring that
      these books are used by the pupils. The more exposure of the children to reading is
      likely to have aided them in acquiring reading skills. In addition, instituting the
      Literacy hour exposes children to the culture ofreading.

Results from Table 8 indicate that there has been an increase in the enrolment o f students
inuniversities and affiliated colleges from 78,107 students in2005/06 to 80,613 studentsin
2006/07, an increase o f 3.2%. The share o f female students universities also increased from
42.3% in 2005/06 to 44.3% in 2006/07.             This increase is attributed to government
sustained implementation of 1.5 additional points for females joining universities andother
tertiary institutions, reinforced by other scholarship schemes that target girls e.g. the
Carnegie Sponsored Female Scholarship Initiative (FSI), etc. However, results indicate
that overall, the share o f females reduced from 41.1% in2005/06 to 39% in2006/07.

(i)     P.l ThematicCurriculum

        In October 2006, preparations for the roll-out of the P.l Thematic Curriculum
        begun with training o f 20 core team members; the Training Manual for the Master
        trainers was reviewed and updated and training o f 50 Master Trainers on the
        Thematic Curriculum was undertaken.

        In December 2006, 1,760 TOTSwho were mainly Centre Coordinating Tutors
        (CCTs) were trained and regional training was conducted in preparation for the
       training o fthe P.1teachers and head teachers.

       In January 2007, 42,500 P.l teachers and head teachers were trained on the
       Thematic Curriculum by the CCTs.

       InMarch 2007, monitoring and support supervision of the implementation of the
       thematic curriculum was undertaken.

(ii)   P.2ThematicCurriculum

       InNovember 2006, P.2 Curriculum was finalized inpreparationfor the piloting in
       the 90 pilot schools. A total o f 270 P.2 teachers were trained and piloting was
       undertakeninFebruary 2007.

       InJune2007, abaseline surveywas conducted. Findingsfromthemonitoring
       exercise ledto organisation o f district cluster meetingfor the teachers to offer
       support to the teachers inthe challenging areas.

       InJuly, comments and observations from the Junemonitoring, were usedto finalise
       the P.2 Curriculum and Teacher's Guide, andmaterial specifications for P.2 were
       developed to facilitate the procurement o f the instructional materials.

(e)     Status

        128,371 (99.51%) primary teachers had accessed the government payroll by April
        2007. However, by September 2007, the total number o f Primary School Teachers
        on the payroll had reduced to 127,694 (98.9%) as a result o f increased number o f
        Primary School Teachers absconding from duty over the past three months. The
        Ministry o f Public Service is tracking the most affected districts to establish the
        cause and come up with mechanisms to curb the problem. The affected Districts are
        Rakai, Nakasongola, Mayuge, Katakwi, Mubende, Amuru and Masindi. An action
        matrix indicating progress to improve primary school teachers' access on the
        payroll i s attached as Table 10.

Undertakingmet.

4.0     GENERALCONCLUSION

      The Review successhlly appraised the progress during the past financial year
      2007/08, and identified strengths and challenges o f the Education and Sports sector.
      Specific issues o f concern were discussed and proposals for hrther improvement
      suggestedand endorsed bythe Review participants.

      The 14thESR concluded that there has been reasonable progress towards meetingthe
      Undertakings agreed upon at the November 2006 Education and Sports Sector
      Review (ESSR). However, there are challenges, particularly in the area of primary
      school completion rates, mainly arising from inefficiencies in the sector. Both the
      efficiency study and the diagnostic study on low completion rates informed the
      action plans for addressing the challenges identified. With the progress made in the
      sector, and the agreed actions for immediate implementation, the outcome o f the
      ESSR will now trigger the release o f Education and Sports Sector Budget Support
      andADB Direct Donor Support Funds.
